</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Haitian_migration_and_influence">Haitian migration and influence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Louisiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Haitian migration and influence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Spanish occupation of Louisiana lasted from 1769 to 1800. Beginning in the 1790s, waves of immigration took place from <a href="/wiki/Saint-Domingue" title="Saint-Domingue">Saint-Domingue</a>, following a slave rebellion that started in 1791. Over the next decade, thousands of migrants landed in Louisiana from the island, including ethnic Europeans, <a href="/wiki/Free_people_of_color" title="Free people of color">free people of color</a>, and African slaves, some of the latter brought in by each free group. They greatly increased the French-speaking population in New Orleans and Louisiana, as well as the number of Africans, and the slaves reinforced African culture in the city. The process of gaining independence in Saint-Domingue was complex, but uprisings continued. In 1803, France pulled out its surviving troops from the island, having suffered the loss of two-thirds sent to the island two years before, mostly to <a href="/wiki/Yellow_fever" title="Yellow fever">yellow fever</a>. In 1804, <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a>, the second republic in the western hemisphere, proclaimed its independence, achieved by slave leaders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Pierre_Cl%C3%A9ment_de_Laussat" title="Pierre Clément de Laussat">Pierre Clément de Laussat</a> (<a href="/wiki/List_of_colonial_governors_of_Louisiana" title="List of colonial governors of Louisiana">Governor</a>, 1803) said: "<a href="/wiki/Saint-Domingue" title="Saint-Domingue">Saint-Domingue</a> was, of all our colonies in the Antilles, the one whose mentality and customs influenced Louisiana the most."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[62]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Anonymous_portrait_of_Jean_Lafitte,_early_19th_century,_Rosenberg_Library,_Galveston,_Texas.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="753" data-file-width="588" height="218" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Anonymous_portrait_of_Jean_Lafitte%2C_early_19th_century%2C_Rosenberg_Library%2C_Galveston%2C_Texas.JPG/170px-Anonymous_portrait_of_Jean_Lafitte%2C_early_19th_century%2C_Rosenberg_Library%2C_Galveston%2C_Texas.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Anonymous_portrait_of_Jean_Lafitte%2C_early_19th_century%2C_Rosenberg_Library%2C_Galveston%2C_Texas.JPG/255px-Anonymous_portrait_of_Jean_Lafitte%2C_early_19th_century%2C_Rosenberg_Library%2C_Galveston%2C_Texas.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Anonymous_portrait_of_Jean_Lafitte%2C_early_19th_century%2C_Rosenberg_Library%2C_Galveston%2C_Texas.JPG/340px-Anonymous_portrait_of_Jean_Lafitte%2C_early_19th_century%2C_Rosenberg_Library%2C_Galveston%2C_Texas.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Anonymous_portrait_of_Jean_Lafitte,_early_19th_century,_Rosenberg_Library,_Galveston,_Texas.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
French pirate <a href="/wiki/Jean_Lafitte" title="Jean Lafitte">Jean Lafitte</a>, who operated in New Orleans, was born in <a href="/wiki/Port-au-Prince" title="Port-au-Prince">Port-au-Prince</a> around 1782.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span id="Purchase_by_the_United_States_(1803)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Purchase_by_the_United_States_.281803.29">Purchase by the United States (1803)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Louisiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Purchase by the United States (1803)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Purchase" title="Louisiana Purchase">Louisiana Purchase</a></div>
<p>When the United States won its independence from Great Britain in 1783, one of its major concerns was having a European power on its western boundary, and the need for unrestricted access to the Mississippi River. As American settlers pushed west, they found that the <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_Mountains" title="Appalachian Mountains">Appalachian Mountains</a> provided a barrier to shipping goods eastward. The easiest way to ship produce was to use a <a href="/wiki/Flatboat" title="Flatboat">flatboat</a> to float it down the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ohio_river" title="Ohio river">Ohio</a> and Mississippi Rivers to the port of New Orleans, from whence goods could be put on ocean-going vessels. The problem with this route was that the Spanish owned both sides of the Mississippi below <a href="/wiki/Natchez,_Mississippi" title="Natchez, Mississippi">Natchez</a>.</p>
<p>Napoleon's ambitions in Louisiana involved the creation of a new empire centered on the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sugar_trade" title="Sugar trade">sugar trade</a>. By the terms of the Treaty of Amiens of 1802, Great Britain returned ownership of the islands of <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guadaloupe" title="Guadaloupe">Guadaloupe</a> to the French. Napoleon looked upon Louisiana as a depot for these sugar islands, and as a buffer to U.S. settlement. In October 1801 he sent a large military force to take back Saint-Domingue, then under control of Toussaint Louverture after a slave rebellion.</p>
<p>When the army led by Napoleon's brother-in-law Leclerc was defeated, Napoleon decided to sell Louisiana.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Louisiane_1800.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="329" data-file-width="383" height="189" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Louisiane_1800.png/220px-Louisiane_1800.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Louisiane_1800.png/330px-Louisiane_1800.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b4/Louisiane_1800.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Louisiane_1800.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of Louisiana in 1800</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Thomas_Jefferson" title="Thomas Jefferson">Thomas Jefferson</a>, third President of the United States, was disturbed by Napoleon's plans to re-establish French colonies in America. With the possession of New Orleans, Napoleon could close the Mississippi to U.S. commerce at any time. Jefferson authorized <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Robert_Livingston_(1746%E2%80%931813)" title="Robert Livingston (1746–1813)">Robert R. Livingston</a>, U.S. Minister to France, to negotiate for the purchase of the City of New Orleans, portions of the east bank of the Mississippi, and free navigation of the river for U.S. commerce. Livingston was authorized to pay up to $2 million.</p>
<p>An official transfer of Louisiana to French ownership had not yet taken place, and Napoleon's deal with the Spanish was a poorly kept secret on the frontier. On October 18, 1802, however, Juan Ventura Morales, Acting Intendant of Louisiana, made public the intention of Spain to revoke the right of deposit at New Orleans for all cargo from the United States. The closure of this vital port to the United States caused anger and consternation. Commerce in the west was virtually blockaded. Historians believe that the revocation of the right of deposit was prompted by abuses by the Americans, particularly smuggling, and not by French intrigues as was believed at the time. President Jefferson ignored public pressure for war with France, and appointed <a href="/wiki/James_Monroe" title="James Monroe">James Monroe</a> a special envoy to Napoleon, to assist in obtaining New Orleans for the United States. Jefferson also raised the authorized expenditure to $10 million.</p>
<p>However, on April 11, 1803, French Foreign Minister <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Talleyrand" title="Talleyrand">Talleyrand</a> surprised Livingston by asking how much the United States was prepared to pay for the <b>entirety</b> of Louisiana, not just New Orleans and the surrounding area (as Livingston's instructions covered). Monroe agreed with Livingston that Napoleon might withdraw this offer at any time (leaving them with no ability to obtain the desired New Orleans area), and that approval from President Jefferson might take months, so Livingston and Monroe decided to open negotiations immediately. By April 30, they closed a deal for the purchase of the entire Louisiana territory of 828,000 square miles (2,100,000 km<sup>2</sup>) for 60 million <a href="/wiki/French_franc" title="French franc">Francs</a> (approximately $15 million).</p>
<p>Part of this sum, $3.5 million, was used to forgive debts owed by France to the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[64]</a></sup> The payment was made in United States <a href="/wiki/Government_bond" title="Government bond">bonds</a>, which Napoleon sold at face value to the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Dutch</a> firm of <a href="/wiki/Hope_%26_Co." title="Hope &amp; Co.">Hope and Company</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Barings_Bank" title="Barings Bank">British banking house of Baring</a>, at a discount of 87½ per each $100 unit. As a result, France received only $8,831,250 in cash for Louisiana. English banker <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Baring,_1st_Baron_Ashburton" title="Alexander Baring, 1st Baron Ashburton">Alexander Baring</a> conferred with Marbois in Paris, shuttled to the United States to pick up the bonds, took them to Britain, and returned to France with the money – which Napoleon used to wage war against Baring's own country.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_USCapitol_-_Louisiana_Purchase,_1803.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2400" data-file-width="3000" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Flickr_-_USCapitol_-_Louisiana_Purchase%2C_1803.jpg/220px-Flickr_-_USCapitol_-_Louisiana_Purchase%2C_1803.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Flickr_-_USCapitol_-_Louisiana_Purchase%2C_1803.jpg/330px-Flickr_-_USCapitol_-_Louisiana_Purchase%2C_1803.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Flickr_-_USCapitol_-_Louisiana_Purchase%2C_1803.jpg/440px-Flickr_-_USCapitol_-_Louisiana_Purchase%2C_1803.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_USCapitol_-_Louisiana_Purchase,_1803.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Louisiana Purchase, 1803</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>When news of the purchase reached the United States, Jefferson was surprised. He had authorized the expenditure of $10 million for a port city, and instead received treaties committing the government to spend $15 million on a land package which would double the size of the country. Jefferson's political opponents in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Federalist_Party_(United_States)" title="Federalist Party (United States)">Federalist Party</a> argued the Louisiana purchase was a worthless desert,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[65]</a></sup> and that the Constitution did not provide for the acquisition of new land or negotiating treaties without the consent of the Senate. What really worried the opposition was the new states which would inevitably be carved from the Louisiana territory, strengthening Western and Southern interests in Congress, and further reducing the influence of New England Federalists in national affairs. President Jefferson was an enthusiastic supporter of westward expansion, and held firm in his support for the treaty. Despite Federalist objections, the U.S. Senate ratified the Louisiana treaty on October 20, 1803.</p>
<p>By statute enacted on October 31, 1803, President Thomas Jefferson was authorized to take possession of the territories ceded by France and provide for initial governance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup> A transfer ceremony was held in New Orleans on November 29, 1803. Since the Louisiana territory had never officially been turned over to the French, the Spanish took down their flag, and the French raised theirs. The following day, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/General_James_Wilkinson" title="General James Wilkinson">General James Wilkinson</a> accepted possession of New Orleans for the United States. A similar ceremony was held in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Louis,_Missouri" title="St. Louis, Missouri">St. Louis</a> on March 9, 1804, when a French tricolor was raised near the river, replacing the Spanish national flag. The following day, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Captain_(U.S._Army)" title="Captain (U.S. Army)">Captain</a> <a href="/wiki/Amos_Stoddard" title="Amos Stoddard">Amos Stoddard</a> of the First U.S. Artillery marched his troops into town and had the American flag run up the fort's flagpole. The Louisiana territory was officially transferred to the United States government, represented by <a href="/wiki/Meriwether_Lewis" title="Meriwether Lewis">Meriwether Lewis</a>.</p>
<p>The Louisiana Territory, purchased for less than 3 cents an acre, doubled the size of the United States overnight, without a war or the loss of a single American life, and set a precedent for the purchase of territory. It opened the way for the eventual expansion of the United States across the continent to the Pacific.</p>
<p>Shortly after the United States took possession, the area was divided into two territories along the <a href="/wiki/33rd_parallel_north" title="33rd parallel north">33rd parallel north</a> on March 26, 1804, thereby organizing the <a href="/wiki/Territory_of_Orleans" title="Territory of Orleans">Territory of Orleans</a> to the south and the <a href="/wiki/District_of_Louisiana" title="District of Louisiana">District of Louisiana</a> (subsequently formed as the <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Territory" title="Louisiana Territory">Louisiana Territory</a>) to the north.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Statehood_(1812)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Statehood_.281812.29">Statehood (1812)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Louisiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Statehood (1812)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Louisiana became the eighteenth U.S. state on April 30, 1812; the Territory of Orleans became the State of Louisiana and the Louisiana Territory was simultaneously renamed the <a href="/wiki/Missouri_Territory" title="Missouri Territory">Missouri Territory</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[68]</a></sup> An area known as the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Parishes" title="Florida Parishes">Florida Parishes</a>, was soon annexed into the state of Louisiana on April 14, 1812.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Secession_and_the_Civil_War_(1860–1865)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Secession_and_the_Civil_War_.281860.E2.80.931865.29">Secession and the Civil War (1860–1865)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Louisiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Secession and the Civil War (1860–1865)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%27Signing_the_Ordinance_of_Secession_of_Louisiana,_January_26,_1861%27,_oil_on_canvas_painting_by_Enoch_Wood_Perry,_Jr.,_1861.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="298" data-file-width="650" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/%27Signing_the_Ordinance_of_Secession_of_Louisiana%2C_January_26%2C_1861%27%2C_oil_on_canvas_painting_by_Enoch_Wood_Perry%2C_Jr.%2C_1861.jpg/300px-%27Signing_the_Ordinance_of_Secession_of_Louisiana%2C_January_26%2C_1861%27%2C_oil_on_canvas_painting_by_Enoch_Wood_Perry%2C_Jr.%2C_1861.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/%27Signing_the_Ordinance_of_Secession_of_Louisiana%2C_January_26%2C_1861%27%2C_oil_on_canvas_painting_by_Enoch_Wood_Perry%2C_Jr.%2C_1861.jpg/450px-%27Signing_the_Ordinance_of_Secession_of_Louisiana%2C_January_26%2C_1861%27%2C_oil_on_canvas_painting_by_Enoch_Wood_Perry%2C_Jr.%2C_1861.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/%27Signing_the_Ordinance_of_Secession_of_Louisiana%2C_January_26%2C_1861%27%2C_oil_on_canvas_painting_by_Enoch_Wood_Perry%2C_Jr.%2C_1861.jpg/600px-%27Signing_the_Ordinance_of_Secession_of_Louisiana%2C_January_26%2C_1861%27%2C_oil_on_canvas_painting_by_Enoch_Wood_Perry%2C_Jr.%2C_1861.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%27Signing_the_Ordinance_of_Secession_of_Louisiana,_January_26,_1861%27,_oil_on_canvas_painting_by_Enoch_Wood_Perry,_Jr.,_1861.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
'Signing the Ordinance of Secession of Louisiana, January 26, 1861', oil on canvas painting, 1861</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:New_Orleans_h76369k.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="529" data-file-width="740" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/New_Orleans_h76369k.jpg/220px-New_Orleans_h76369k.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/New_Orleans_h76369k.jpg/330px-New_Orleans_h76369k.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/New_Orleans_h76369k.jpg/440px-New_Orleans_h76369k.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:New_Orleans_h76369k.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Forts_Jackson_and_St._Philip" title="Battle of Forts Jackson and St. Philip"><i>Capture of New Orleans</i></a>, April 1862, colored lithograph of engraving</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>According to the 1860 census, 331,726 people were enslaved, nearly 47% of the state's total population of 708,002.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[70]</a></sup> The strong economic interest of elite whites in maintaining the slave society contributed to Louisiana's decision to secede from the Union in 1861. It followed other Southern states in seceding after the election of <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln" title="Abraham Lincoln">Abraham Lincoln</a> as <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President of the United States</a>. Louisiana's secession was announced on January 26, 1861, and it became part of the <a href="/wiki/Confederate_States_of_America" title="Confederate States of America">Confederate States of America</a>.</p>
<p>The state was quickly defeated in the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">Civil War</a>, a result of Union strategy to cut the Confederacy in two by seizing the Mississippi. Federal troops captured New Orleans on April 25, 1862. Because a large part of the population had Union sympathies (or compatible commercial interests), the Federal government took the unusual step of designating the areas of Louisiana under Federal control as a state within the Union, with its own elected representatives to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Congress" title="U.S. Congress">U.S. Congress</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> US troops stationed in New Orleans complained of insults by its women.</p>
<h3><span id="Post-Civil_War_to_mid-20th_century_(1865–1945)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-Civil_War_to_mid-20th_century_.281865.E2.80.931945.29">Post-Civil War to mid-20th century (1865–1945)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Louisiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Post-Civil War to mid-20th century (1865–1945)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Following the Civil War and emancipation of slaves, violence rose in the South as the war was carried on by insurgent private and paramilitary groups. Initially state legislatures were dominated by former Confederates, who passed Black Codes to regulate <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freedmen" title="Freedmen">freedmen</a> and generally refused to give the vote. They refused to extend voting rights to African Americans who had been free before the war and had sometimes obtained education and property (as in New Orleans.) Following the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Memphis_Riots_of_1866" title="Memphis Riots of 1866">Memphis Riots of 1866</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Riot" title="New Orleans Riot">New Orleans Riot</a> the same year, the Fourteenth Amendment was passed that provided suffrage and full citizenship for freedmen. Congress passed the Reconstruction Act, establishing military districts for those states where conditions were considered the worst, including Louisiana. It was grouped with <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a> in what was administered as the <a href="/wiki/Fifth_Military_District" title="Fifth Military District">Fifth Military District</a>.</p>
<p>African Americans began to live as citizens with some measure of equality before the law. Both <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freedmen" title="Freedmen">freedmen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Free_people_of_color" title="Free people of color">people of color</a> who had been free before the war began to make more advances in education, family stability and jobs. At the same time, there was tremendous social volatility in the aftermath of war, with many whites actively resisting defeat and the free labor market. White <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Insurgents" title="Insurgents">insurgents</a> mobilized to enforce <a href="/wiki/White_supremacy" title="White supremacy">white supremacy</a>, first in <a href="/wiki/Ku_Klux_Klan" title="Ku Klux Klan">Ku Klux Klan</a> chapters.</p>
<p>By 1877, when federal forces were withdrawn, white Democrats in Louisiana and other states had regained control of state legislatures, often by paramilitary groups such as the <a href="/wiki/White_League" title="White League">White League</a>, which suppressed black voting through intimidation and violence. Following Mississippi's example in 1890, in 1898, the white Democratic, planter-dominated legislature passed a new constitution that effectively <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disfranchisement_after_Reconstruction_era" title="Disfranchisement after Reconstruction era">disenfranchised</a> blacks and people of color, by raising barriers to voter registration, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Poll_tax_(United_States)" title="Poll tax (United States)">poll taxes</a>, residency requirements and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Literacy_tests" title="Literacy tests">literacy tests</a>. The effect was immediate and long lasting. In 1896, there were 130,334 black voters on the rolls and about the same number of white voters, in proportion to the state population, which was evenly divided.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>The state population in 1900 was 47% African-American: a total of 652,013 citizens. Many in New Orleans were descendants of Creoles of color, the sizeable population of <a href="/wiki/Free_people_of_color" title="Free people of color">free people of color</a> before the Civil War.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup> By 1900, two years after the new constitution, only 5,320 black voters were registered in the state. Because of disfranchisement, by 1910 there were only 730 black voters (less than 0.5 percent of eligible African-American men), despite advances in education and literacy among blacks and people of color.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[73]</a></sup> Blacks were excluded from the political system and also unable to serve on juries. White Democrats had established one-party Democratic rule, which they maintained in the state for decades deep into the 20th century until after Congressional passage of the 1965 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voting_Rights_Act" title="Voting Rights Act">Voting Rights Act</a> provided federal oversight and enforcement of the constitutional right to vote.</p>
<p>In the early decades of the 20th century, thousands of African Americans left Louisiana in the <a href="/wiki/Great_Migration_(African_American)" title="Great Migration (African American)">Great Migration</a> north to industrial cities for jobs and education, and to escape Jim Crow society and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lynchings" title="Lynchings">lynchings</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Boll_weevil" title="Boll weevil">boll weevil</a> infestation and agricultural problems cost many sharecroppers and farmers their jobs. The mechanization of agriculture also reduced the need for laborers. Beginning in the 1940s, blacks went West to California for jobs in its expanding defense industries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup></p>
<p>During some of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>, Louisiana was led by Governor <a href="/wiki/Huey_Long" title="Huey Long">Huey Long</a>. He was elected to office on populist appeal. His public works projects provided thousands of jobs to people in need, and he supported education and increased suffrage for poor whites, but Long was criticized for his allegedly demogogic and autocratic style. He extended patronage control through every branch of Louisiana's state government. Especially controversial were his plans for wealth redistribution in the state. Long's rule ended abruptly when the governor was assassinated in the state capitol in 1935.</p>
<h3><span id="Post-World_War_II_(1945–)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-World_War_II_.281945.E2.80.93.29">Post-World War II (1945–)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Louisiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Post-World War II (1945–)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Mobilization for <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> created jobs in the state. Thousands of other workers, black and white alike, migrated to California for better jobs in its burgeoning defense industry. Many African Americans left the state in the <a href="/wiki/Second_Great_Migration_(African_American)" title="Second Great Migration (African American)">Second Great Migration</a>, from the 1940s through the 1960s. The mechanization of agriculture in the 1930s had sharply cut the need for laborers. They sought skilled jobs in the defense industry in California, better education for their children, and living opportunities in communities where they could vote.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the 1950s the state created new requirements for a citizenship test for voter registration. Despite opposition by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dixiecrats" title="Dixiecrats">States Rights Party</a>, downstate black voters began to increase their rate of registration, which also reflected the growth of their middle classes. Gradually black voter registration and turnout increased to 20% and more, and it was 32% in 1964, when the first national civil rights legislation of the era was passed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup> The percentage of black voters ranged widely in the state during these years, from 93.8% in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evangeline_Parish" title="Evangeline Parish">Evangeline Parish</a> to 1.7% in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tensas_Parish" title="Tensas Parish">Tensas Parish</a>, for instance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thernstrom_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-thernstrom-78">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>Violent attacks on civil rights activists in two mill towns were catalysts to the founding of the first two chapters of the <a href="/wiki/Deacons_for_Defense_and_Justice" title="Deacons for Defense and Justice">Deacons for Defense and Justice</a> in late 1964 and early 1965, in <a href="/wiki/Jonesboro,_Louisiana" title="Jonesboro, Louisiana">Jonesboro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bogalusa,_Louisiana" title="Bogalusa, Louisiana">Bogalusa</a>, respectively. Made up of veterans of World War II and the Korean War, they were armed self-defense groups established to protect activists and their families. Continued violent white resistance in Bogalusa to blacks trying to use public facilities in 1965, following passage of the <a href="/wiki/Civil_Rights_Act_of_1964" title="Civil Rights Act of 1964">Civil Rights Act of 1964</a>, caused the federal government to order local police to protect the activists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nyt_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-79">[78]</a></sup> Other chapters were formed in Louisiana, Mississippi, and Alabama.</p>
<p>By 1960 the proportion of African Americans in Louisiana had dropped to 32%. The 1,039,207 black citizens were suppressed by segregation and disfranchisement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[79]</a></sup> African Americans continued to suffer disproportionate discriminatory application of the state's voter registration rules. Because of better opportunities elsewhere, from 1965 to 1970, blacks continued to migrate from Louisiana, for a net loss of more than 37,000 people. Based on official census figures, the African-American population in 1970 stood at 1,085,109, a net gain of more than 46,000 people compared to 1960. During the latter period, some people began to migrate to cities of the <a href="/wiki/New_South" title="New South">New South</a> for opportunities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[80]</a></sup> Since that period, blacks entered the political system and began to be elected to office, as well as having other opportunities.</p>
<p>On 21st May 1919, the <a href="/wiki/Nineteenth_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Nineteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution">Nineteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution</a>, giving women full rights to vote, was passed at a national level, and was made the law throughout the United States on 18th August 1920. Louisiana finally ratified the amendment on 11th June 1970.</p>
<p>In August 2005, New Orleans and many other low-lying parts of the state along the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a> were hit by the catastrophic <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">Hurricane Katrina</a>. It caused widespread damage due to breaching of levees and large-scale flooding of more than 80% of the city. Officials issued warnings to evacuate the city and nearby areas, but tens of thousands of people, mostly African Americans, stayed behind, many of them stranded, and suffered through the damage of the widespread floodwaters.</p>
<p>In August 2016, <a href="/wiki/2016_Louisiana_floods" title="2016 Louisiana floods">an unnamed storm</a> dumped trillions of gallons of rain on southern Louisiana, including the cities of <a href="/wiki/Denham_Springs,_Louisiana" title="Denham Springs, Louisiana">Denham Springs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baton_Rouge,_Louisiana" title="Baton Rouge, Louisiana">Baton Rouge</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lafayette,_Louisiana" title="Lafayette, Louisiana">Lafayette</a>, causing catastrophic flooding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup> An estimated 110,000 homes were damaged<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup> and thousands of residents were displaced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-84">[83]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Louisiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">United States Census Bureau</a> estimates that the population of Louisiana was 4,670,724 on July 1, 2015, a 3.03% increase since the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 United States Census</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstUS_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-PopEstUS-86">[85]</a></sup> The population density of the state is 104.9 people per square mile.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2010.census.gov_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-2010.census.gov-87">[86]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Center_of_population" title="Center of population">center of population</a> of Louisiana is located in <a href="/wiki/Pointe_Coupee_Parish,_Louisiana" title="Pointe Coupee Parish, Louisiana">Pointe Coupee Parish</a>, in the city of <a href="/wiki/New_Roads,_Louisiana" title="New Roads, Louisiana">New Roads</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[87]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 United States Census</a>, 5.4% of the population aged 5 and older spoke <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language_in_the_United_States" title="Spanish language in the United States">Spanish</a> at home, up from 3.5% in 2000; and 4.5% spoke French (including <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_French" title="Louisiana French">Louisiana French</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louisiana_Creole_French" title="Louisiana Creole French">Louisiana Creole</a>), down from 4.8% in 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[89]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Race_and_ethnicity">Race and ethnicity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Louisiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Race and ethnicity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to the US census estimates, the population of Louisiana in 2014 was:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/White_Americans" title="White Americans">White Americans</a> – 63.4% (59.3% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-Hispanic_white" title="Non-Hispanic white">non-Hispanic white</a>, 4.1% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_Hispanic" title="White Hispanic">White Hispanic</a>)</li>
<li>Black or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_American" title="African American">African American</a> – 32.5%</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_American" title="Asian American">Asian</a> – 1.8%</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multiracial_American" title="Multiracial American">Multiracial American</a> – 1.5%</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">Native American</a> – 0.8%</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hispanic" title="Hispanic">Hispanic</a> or <a href="/wiki/Latino" title="Latino">Latino</a> of any race – 4.8%</li>
</ul>
<p>The major ancestry groups of Louisiana are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_American" title="African American">African American</a> (30.4%), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French-American" title="French-American">French</a> (16.8%), <a href="/wiki/Americans" title="Americans">American</a> (9.5%), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German-American" title="German-American">German</a> (8.3%), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irish-American" title="Irish-American">Irish</a> (7.5%), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/English-American" title="English-American">English</a> (6.6%), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_American" title="Italian American">Italian</a> (4.8%) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scottish-American" title="Scottish-American">Scottish</a> (1.1%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 2011, 49.0% of Louisiana's population younger than age 1 were minorities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Louisiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louisiana_locations_by_per_capita_income" title="Louisiana locations by per capita income">Louisiana locations by per capita income</a></div>
<p>The total <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gross_state_product" title="Gross state product">gross state product</a> in 2010 for Louisiana was US$213.6 billion, placing it 24th in the nation. Its <a href="/wiki/Per_capita_personal_income_in_the_United_States" title="Per capita personal income in the United States">per capita personal income</a> is $30,952, ranking 41st in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2014, Louisiana was ranked as one of the most small business friendly states, based on a study drawing upon data from over 12,000 small business owners.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup></p>
<p>The state's principal agricultural products include seafood (it is the biggest producer of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crawfish" title="Crawfish">crawfish</a> in the world, supplying approximately 90%), <a href="/wiki/Cotton" title="Cotton">cotton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soybean" title="Soybean">soybeans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cattle" title="Cattle">cattle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">sugarcane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poultry" title="Poultry">poultry</a> and eggs, <a href="/wiki/Dairy" title="Dairy">dairy</a> products, and <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">rice</a>. Industry generates chemical products, <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">petroleum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Coal" title="Coal">coal</a> products, processed foods and transportation equipment, and <a href="/wiki/Paper" title="Paper">paper</a> products. Tourism is an important element in the economy, especially in the New Orleans area.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Port_of_South_Louisiana" title="Port of South Louisiana">Port of South Louisiana</a>, located on the <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">Mississippi River</a> between New Orleans and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baton_Rouge" title="Baton Rouge">Baton Rouge</a>, is the largest volume shipping <a href="/wiki/Port" title="Port">port</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Western_Hemisphere" title="Western Hemisphere">Western Hemisphere</a> and 4th largest in the world, as well as the largest <a href="/wiki/Bulk_cargo" title="Bulk cargo">bulk cargo</a> port in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[100]</a></sup></p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Orleans,_Louisiana" title="New Orleans, Louisiana">New Orleans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shreveport,_Louisiana" title="Shreveport, Louisiana">Shreveport</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Baton_Rouge,_Louisiana" title="Baton Rouge, Louisiana">Baton Rouge</a> are home to a thriving film industry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[101]</a></sup> State financial incentives since 2002 and aggressive promotion have given Louisiana the nickname "Hollywood South". Because of its distinctive culture within the United States, only <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a> is Louisiana's rival in popularity as a setting for <a href="/wiki/Reality_television" title="Reality television">reality television</a> programs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-robertson20130516_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-robertson20130516-103">[102]</a></sup> In late 2007 and early 2008, a 300,000-square-foot (28,000 m<sup>2</sup>) film studio was scheduled to open in <a href="/wiki/Trem%C3%A9" title="Tremé">Tremé</a>, with state-of-the-art production facilities, and a film training institute.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[103]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tabasco_sauce" title="Tabasco sauce">Tabasco sauce</a>, which is marketed by one of the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>' biggest producers of hot sauce, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/McIlhenny_Company" title="McIlhenny Company">McIlhenny Company</a>, originated on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Avery_Island" title="Avery Island">Avery Island</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[104]</a></sup></p>
<p>Louisiana has three personal <a href="/wiki/Income_tax" title="Income tax">income tax</a> brackets, ranging from 2% to 6%. The <a href="/wiki/Sales_tax" title="Sales tax">sales tax</a> rate is 4%: a 3.97% Louisiana sales tax and a .03% Louisiana Tourism Promotion District sales tax. Political subdivisions also levy their own sales tax in addition to the state fees. The state also has a <a href="/wiki/Use_tax" title="Use tax">use tax</a>, which includes 4% to be distributed by the Department of Revenue to local governments. Property taxes are assessed and collected at the local level. Louisiana is a subsidized state, receiving $1.44 from the federal government for every dollar paid in.</p>
<p>Tourism and culture are major players in Louisiana's economy, earning an estimated $5.2 billion per year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[105]</a></sup> Louisiana also hosts many important cultural events, such as the World Cultural Economic Forum, which is held annually in the fall at the <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Morial_Convention_Center" title="New Orleans Morial Convention Center">New Orleans Morial Convention Center</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[106]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of July 2017, the state's unemployment rate was 5.3%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Federal_subsidies_and_spending">Federal subsidies and spending</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Louisiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Federal subsidies and spending">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Louisiana taxpayers receive more federal funding per dollar of federal taxes paid compared to the average state. Per dollar of federal tax collected in 2005, Louisiana citizens received approximately $1.78 in the way of federal spending. This ranks the state fourth highest nationally and represents a rise from 1995 when Louisiana received $1.35 per dollar of taxes in federal spending (ranked seventh nationally). Neighboring states and the amount of federal spending received per dollar of federal tax collected were: Texas ($0.94), Arkansas ($1.41), and Mississippi ($2.02). Federal spending in 2005 and subsequent years since has been exceptionally high due to the recovery from Hurricane Katrina. <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20090706135847/http://www.taxfoundation.org/research/topic/31.html" rel="nofollow">Tax Foundation</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Louisiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gulf_Oil_Spill_Creeps_Towards_Mississippi_Delta.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3112" data-file-width="5780" height="118" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Gulf_Oil_Spill_Creeps_Towards_Mississippi_Delta.jpg/220px-Gulf_Oil_Spill_Creeps_Towards_Mississippi_Delta.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Gulf_Oil_Spill_Creeps_Towards_Mississippi_Delta.jpg/330px-Gulf_Oil_Spill_Creeps_Towards_Mississippi_Delta.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Gulf_Oil_Spill_Creeps_Towards_Mississippi_Delta.jpg/440px-Gulf_Oil_Spill_Creeps_Towards_Mississippi_Delta.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gulf_Oil_Spill_Creeps_Towards_Mississippi_Delta.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The oil slick just off the Louisiana coast on April 30, 2010. The <a href="/wiki/Deepwater_Horizon_oil_spill" title="Deepwater Horizon oil spill">Deepwater Horizon oil spill</a> is now considered the biggest environmental disaster in U.S. history.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Louisiana is rich in <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">petroleum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a>. Petroleum and gas deposits are found in abundance both onshore and offshore in State-owned waters. In addition, vast petroleum and natural gas reserves are found offshore from Louisiana in the federally administered <a href="/wiki/Outer_Continental_Shelf" title="Outer Continental Shelf">Outer Continental Shelf</a> (OCS) in the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a>. According to the <a href="/wiki/Energy_Information_Administration" title="Energy Information Administration">Energy Information Administration</a>, the Gulf of Mexico OCS is the largest U.S. petroleum-producing region. Excluding the Gulf of Mexico OCS, Louisiana ranks fourth in petroleum production and is home to about 2 percent of total U.S. petroleum reserves.</p>
<p>Louisiana's natural gas reserves account for about 5 percent of the U.S. total. The recent discovery of the <a href="/wiki/Haynesville_Shale" title="Haynesville Shale">Haynesville Shale</a> formation in parts of or all of Caddo, Bossier, Bienville, Sabine, De Soto, Red River, and Natchitoches parishes have made it the world's fourth largest gas field with some wells initially producing over 25 million cubic feet of gas daily.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[108]</a></sup></p>
<p>Louisiana was the first site of <a href="/wiki/Oil_well" title="Oil well">petroleum drilling</a> over water in the world, on <a href="/wiki/Caddo_Lake" title="Caddo Lake">Caddo Lake</a> in the northwest corner of the state. The petroleum and gas industry, as well as its subsidiary industries such as transport and <a href="/wiki/Oil_refinery" title="Oil refinery">refining</a>, have dominated Louisiana's economy since the 1940s. Beginning in 1950, Louisiana was sued several times by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_the_Interior" title="United States Department of the Interior">U.S. Interior Department</a>, in efforts by the <a href="/wiki/Federal_government_of_the_United_States" title="Federal government of the United States">federal government</a> to strip Louisiana of its submerged land property rights. These control vast stores of reservoirs of petroleum and natural gas.</p>
<p>When petroleum and gas <a href="/wiki/1973_oil_crisis" title="1973 oil crisis">boomed</a> in the 1970s, so did Louisiana's economy. The Louisiana economy as well as its politics of the last half-century cannot be understood without thoroughly accounting for the influence of the petroleum and gas industries. Since the 1980s, these industries' headquarters have consolidated in <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a>, but many of the jobs that operate or provide logistical support to the U.S. Gulf of Mexico crude-oil-and-gas industry remained in Louisiana as of 2010<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Louisiana&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.</p>

<tr>
<td style="padding:0 0.1em 0.4em">
<div class="NavFrame collapsed" style="border:none;padding:0">
<div class="NavHead" style="font-size:105%;background:transparent;text-align:left"><a href="/wiki/Political_division" title="Political division">Political Subdivisions</a></div>
<div class="NavContent" style="font-size:105%;padding:0.2em 0 0.4em;text-align:center;text-align:left">
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_parishes_in_Louisiana" title="List of parishes in Louisiana">Parishes</a> (64)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_municipalities_in_Louisiana" title="List of municipalities in Louisiana">Municipalities</a> (303)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_school_districts_in_Louisiana" title="List of school districts in Louisiana">School districts</a></li>
</ul>
</div>
</div>
</td>
</tr>

<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Louisiana_State_Capitol_Building.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="12708" data-file-width="11753" height="238" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Louisiana_State_Capitol_Building.jpg/220px-Louisiana_State_Capitol_Building.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Louisiana_State_Capitol_Building.jpg/330px-Louisiana_State_Capitol_Building.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Louisiana_State_Capitol_Building.jpg/440px-Louisiana_State_Capitol_Building.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

The <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_State_Capitol" title="Louisiana State Capitol">Louisiana State Capitol</a> in Baton Rouge, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heights_of_state_capitols" title="Heights of state capitols">tallest state capitol building</a> in the United States.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LAGovMansion.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="2000" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/LAGovMansion.JPG/220px-LAGovMansion.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/LAGovMansion.JPG/330px-LAGovMansion.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/LAGovMansion.JPG/440px-LAGovMansion.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LAGovMansion.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Louisiana Governor's Mansion</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1849, the state moved the capital from New Orleans to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baton_Rouge" title="Baton Rouge">Baton Rouge</a>. <a href="/wiki/Donaldsonville,_Louisiana" title="Donaldsonville, Louisiana">Donaldsonville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Opelousas,_Louisiana" title="Opelousas, Louisiana">Opelousas</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Shreveport,_Louisiana" title="Shreveport, Louisiana">Shreveport</a> have briefly served as the seat of Louisiana state government. The <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_State_Capitol" title="Louisiana State Capitol">Louisiana State Capitol</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Governor%27s_Mansion" title="Louisiana Governor's Mansion">Louisiana Governor's Mansion</a> are both located in Baton Rouge. The <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Supreme_Court" title="Louisiana Supreme Court">Louisiana Supreme Court</a>, however, did not move to Baton Rouge but remains headquartered in New Orleans.</p>
<p>Louisiana and California (whose supreme court is seated in San Francisco) are the only two states whose high courts are not headquartered in the state capital.</p>
<p>The current Louisiana governor is <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democrat</a> <a href="/wiki/John_Bel_Edwards" title="John Bel Edwards">John Bel Edwards</a>.The current <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">United States Senators</a> are Republicans <a href="/wiki/John_Neely_Kennedy" title="John Neely Kennedy">John Neely Kennedy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bill_Cassidy" title="Bill Cassidy">Bill Cassidy</a>. Louisiana has six <a href="/wiki/Congressional_district" title="Congressional district">congressional districts</a> and is represented in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">U.S. House of Representatives</a> by five Republicans and one Democrat. Louisiana had eight votes in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Electoral_College" title="United States Electoral College">Electoral College</a> for the 2012 election. It lost one House seat due to stagnant population growth in the 2010 Census.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Louisiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Louisiana is divided into 64 <a href="/wiki/Parish_(administrative_division)" title="Parish (administrative division)">parishes</a> (the equivalent of <a href="/wiki/County_(United_States)" title="County (United States)">counties</a> in most other states).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nativeamericans_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-nativeamericans-110">[109]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_parishes_in_Louisiana" title="List of parishes in Louisiana">List of parishes in Louisiana</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louisiana_census_statistical_areas" title="Louisiana census statistical areas">Louisiana census statistical areas</a></li>
</ul>
<p>Most parishes have an elected government known as the Police Jury, dating from the colonial days. It is the legislative and executive government of the parish, and is elected by the voters. Its members are called Jurors, and together they elect a President as their chairman.</p>
<p>A more limited number of parishes operate under <a href="/wiki/Home_rule" title="Home rule">home rule</a> charters, electing various forms of government. This include mayor–council, council–manager (in which the council hires a professional operating manager for the parish), and others.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Civil_law">Civil law</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Louisiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Civil law">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Louisiana political and legal structure has maintained several elements from the times of French and Spanish governance. One is the use of the term "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parish_(Louisiana)" title="Parish (Louisiana)">parish</a>" (from the French: <i>paroisse</i>) in place of "<a href="/wiki/County_(United_States)" title="County (United States)">county</a>" for administrative subdivision. Another is the legal system of <a href="/wiki/Civil_law_(legal_system)" title="Civil law (legal system)">civil law</a> based on French, German, and Spanish <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legal_code" title="Legal code">legal codes</a> and ultimately <a href="/wiki/Roman_law" title="Roman law">Roman law</a>, as opposed to English <a href="/wiki/Common_law" title="Common law">common law</a>.</p>
<p>Louisiana's civil law system is what the majority of nations in the world use, especially in Europe and its former colonies, excluding those that derive from the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a>. However, it is incorrect to equate the Louisiana Civil Code with the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Code" title="Napoleonic Code">Napoleonic Code</a>. Although the Napoleonic Code and Louisiana law draw from common legal roots, the Napoleonic Code was never in force in Louisiana, as it was enacted in 1804, after the United States had <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Purchase" title="Louisiana Purchase">purchased</a> and annexed Louisiana in 1803.</p>
<p>While the Louisiana Civil Code of 1808 has been continuously revised and updated since its enactment, it is still considered the controlling authority in the state. Differences are found between Louisianan civil law and the common law found in the other U.S. states. While some of these differences have been bridged due to the strong influence of common law tradition,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kinsellalaw_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-kinsellalaw-111">[110]</a></sup> the civil law tradition is still deeply rooted in most aspects of Louisiana private law. Thus property, contractual, business entities structure, much of civil procedure, and family law, as well as some aspects of criminal law, are still based mostly on traditional Roman legal thinking.</p>
<p>Model Codes, such as the <a href="/wiki/Uniform_Commercial_Code" title="Uniform Commercial Code">Uniform Commercial Code</a>, which are adopted by most states within the union including Louisiana, are based on civil legal thought, which is essentially <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deductive" title="Deductive">deductive</a>, as opposed to the common law, which is <a href="/wiki/Inductive_reasoning" title="Inductive reasoning">inductive</a>. In the civil law tradition, the legislative body agrees <i>a priori</i> on the general principles to be followed. When a set of facts are brought before a judge, he deduces the court's ruling by comparing the facts of the individual case to the law.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marriage">Marriage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Louisiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Marriage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1997, Louisiana became the first state to offer the option of a traditional marriage or a <a href="/wiki/Covenant_marriage" title="Covenant marriage">covenant marriage</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[111]</a></sup> In a covenant marriage, the couple waives their right to a "no-fault" divorce after six months of separation, which is available in a traditional marriage. To divorce under a covenant marriage, a couple must demonstrate cause. Marriages between ascendants and descendants, and marriages between collaterals within the fourth degree (i.e., siblings, aunt and nephew, uncle and niece, first cousins) are prohibited.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[112]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage" title="Same-sex marriage">Same-sex marriages</a> were prohibited by statute,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[113]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup> but the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">Supreme Court</a> declared such bans unconstitutional in 2015, in its ruling in <i><a href="/wiki/Obergefell_v._Hodges" title="Obergefell v. Hodges">Obergefell v. Hodges</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Louisiana" title="LGBT rights in Louisiana">Same-sex marriages are now performed statewide</a>. Louisiana is a <a href="/wiki/Community_property" title="Community property">community property</a> state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[115]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Elections">Elections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Louisiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Elections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Louisiana" title="Elections in Louisiana">Elections in Louisiana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Political_party_strength_in_Louisiana" title="Political party strength in Louisiana">Political party strength in Louisiana</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:307px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:United_States_presidential_election_in_Louisiana,_2016.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3201" data-file-width="2904" height="336" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/United_States_presidential_election_in_Louisiana%2C_2016.svg/305px-United_States_presidential_election_in_Louisiana%2C_2016.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/United_States_presidential_election_in_Louisiana%2C_2016.svg/458px-United_States_presidential_election_in_Louisiana%2C_2016.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/United_States_presidential_election_in_Louisiana%2C_2016.svg/610px-United_States_presidential_election_in_Louisiana%2C_2016.svg.png 2x" width="305"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:United_States_presidential_election_in_Louisiana,_2016.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treemap" title="Treemap">Treemap</a> of the popular vote by county, 2016 presidential election.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>From 1898 to 1965, a period when Louisiana had effectively <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disfranchisement_after_the_Civil_War" title="Disfranchisement after the Civil War">disfranchised</a> most African Americans and many poor whites by provisions of a new constitution,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GWUweb_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-GWUweb-117">[116]</a></sup> this was essentially a one-party state dominated by white Democrats. Elites had control in the early 20th century, before populist <a href="/wiki/Huey_Long" title="Huey Long">Huey Long</a> came to power as governor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cashman_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cashman-118">[117]</a></sup> In multiple acts of resistance, blacks left behind the segregation, violence and oppression of the state and moved out to seek better opportunities in northern and western industrial cities during the <a href="/wiki/Great_Migration_(African_American)" title="Great Migration (African American)">Great Migrations</a> of 1910–1970, markedly reducing their proportion of population in Louisiana. The franchise for whites was expanded somewhat during these decades, but blacks remained essentially disfranchised until after the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Civil_Rights_Movement" title="Civil Rights Movement">Civil Rights Movement</a> of the mid-20th century, gaining enforcement of their constitutional rights through passage by Congress of the <a href="/wiki/Voting_Rights_Act_of_1965" title="Voting Rights Act of 1965">Voting Rights Act of 1965</a>.</p>
<p>Since the 1960s, when civil rights legislation was passed under President <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lyndon_Johnson" title="Lyndon Johnson">Lyndon Johnson</a> to protect voting and civil rights, most African Americans in the state have affiliated with the Democratic Party. In the same years, many white social conservatives have moved to support Republican Party candidates in national, gubernatorial and statewide elections. In 2004, <a href="/wiki/David_Vitter" title="David Vitter">David Vitter</a> was the first Republican in Louisiana to be popularly elected as a U.S. Senator. The previous Republican Senator, <a href="/wiki/John_S._Harris" title="John S. Harris">John S. Harris</a>, who took office in 1868 during Reconstruction, was chosen by the state legislature under the rules of the 19th century.</p>
<p>Louisiana is unique among U.S. states in using a system for its state and local elections similar to that of modern <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>. All candidates, regardless of party affiliation, run in a <a href="/wiki/Nonpartisan_blanket_primary" title="Nonpartisan blanket primary">nonpartisan blanket primary</a> (or "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jungle_primary" title="Jungle primary">jungle primary</a>") on Election Day. If no candidate has more than 50% of the vote, the two candidates with the highest vote totals compete in a runoff election approximately one month later. This run-off did not take into account party identification; therefore, it was not uncommon for a Democrat to be in a runoff with a fellow Democrat or a Republican to be in a runoff with a fellow Republican.</p>
<p>Congressional races have also been held under the jungle primary system. All other states (except <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Washington_Initiative_872_(2004)" title="Washington Initiative 872 (2004)">Washington</a> and <a href="/wiki/California_Proposition_14_(2010)" title="California Proposition 14 (2010)">California</a>) use single-party primaries followed by a general election between party candidates, each conducted by either a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plurality_voting_system" title="Plurality voting system">plurality voting system</a> or <a href="/wiki/Two-round_system" title="Two-round system">runoff voting</a>, to elect Senators, Representatives, and statewide officials. Between 2008 and 2010, federal <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">congressional</a> elections were run under a closed primary system – limited to registered party members. However, upon the passage of House Bill 292, Louisiana again adopted a nonpartisan blanket primary for its federal congressional elections.</p>
<p>Louisiana has six seats in the U.S. House of Representatives, five of which are currently held by Republicans and one by a Democrat. The state lost a House seat at the end of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/112th_Congress" title="112th Congress">112th Congress</a> due to stagnant population growth as recorded by the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 United States Census</a>. Louisiana is not classified as a "<a href="/wiki/Swing_state" title="Swing state">swing state</a>" for future presidential elections, as since the late 20th century, it has regularly supported Republican candidates. The state's two U.S. senators are <a href="/wiki/Bill_Cassidy" title="Bill Cassidy">Bill Cassidy</a> (R) <a href="/wiki/John_Neely_Kennedy" title="John Neely Kennedy">John Neely Kennedy</a> (R).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_enforcement">Law enforcement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Louisiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Law enforcement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_law_enforcement_agencies_in_Louisiana" title="List of law enforcement agencies in Louisiana">List of law enforcement agencies in Louisiana</a></div>
<p>Louisiana's statewide police force is the <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_State_Police" title="Louisiana State Police">Louisiana State Police</a>. It began in 1922 with the creation of the Highway Commission. In 1927, a second branch, the Bureau of Criminal Investigations, was formed. In 1932, the State Highway Patrol was authorized to carry weapons.</p>
<p>On July 28, 1936, the two branches were consolidated to form the Louisiana Department of State Police; its motto was "courtesy, loyalty, service". In 1942, this office was abolished and became a division of the Department of Public Safety, called the Louisiana State Police. In 1988, the Criminal Investigation Bureau was reorganized.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[118]</a></sup> Its troopers have statewide jurisdiction with power to enforce all laws of the state, including city and parish ordinances. Each year, they patrol over 12 million miles (20 million km) of roadway and arrest about 10,000 impaired drivers. The State Police are primarily a traffic enforcement agency, with other sections that delve into trucking safety, narcotics enforcement, and gaming oversight.</p>
<p>The elected sheriff in each parish is the chief law enforcement officer in the parish. They are the keepers of the local parish prisons, which house felony and misdemeanor prisoners. They are the primary criminal patrol and first responder agency in all matters criminal and civil. They are also the official tax collectors in each parish.</p>
<p>The sheriffs are responsible for general law enforcement in their respective parishes. Orleans Parish is an exception, as the general law enforcement duties fall to the New Orleans Police Department. Before 2010, Orleans parish was the only parish to have two sheriff's offices. Orleans Parish divided sheriffs' duties between criminal and civil, with a different elected sheriff overseeing each aspect. In 2006, a bill was passed which eventually consolidated the two sheriff's departments into one parish sheriff responsible for both civil and criminal matters.</p>
<p>In 2015, Louisiana had a higher murder rate (10.3 per 100,000) than any other state in the country for the 27th straight year. Louisiana is the only state with an annual average murder rate (13.6 per 100,000) at least twice as high as the U.S. annual average (6.6 per 100,000) during that period, according to Bureau of Justice Statistics from FBI Uniform Crime Reports. In a different kind of criminal activity, the <i><a href="/wiki/Chicago_Tribune" title="Chicago Tribune">Chicago Tribune</a></i> reports that Louisiana is the most corrupt state in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Times_Picayune" title="Times Picayune">Times Picayune</a></i>, Louisiana is the prison capital of the world. Many <a href="/wiki/Private_prison" title="Private prison">for-profit</a> private prisons and sheriff-owned prisons have been built and operate here. Louisiana's incarceration rate is nearly five times Iran's, 13 times China's and 20 times <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany's</a>. Minorities are incarcerated at rates disproportionate to their share of the state's population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Judiciary">Judiciary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Louisiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Judiciary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Judiciary_of_Louisiana" title="Judiciary of Louisiana">judiciary of Louisiana</a> is defined under the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Louisiana" title="Constitution of Louisiana">Constitution</a> and <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Louisiana" title="Law of Louisiana">law of Louisiana</a> and is composed of the <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Supreme_Court" title="Louisiana Supreme Court">Louisiana Supreme Court</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Circuit_Courts_of_Appeal" title="Louisiana Circuit Courts of Appeal">Louisiana Circuit Courts of Appeal</a>, the District Courts, the Justice of the Peace Courts, the Mayor's Courts, the City Courts, and the Parish Courts. The Chief Justice of the Louisiana Supreme Court is the chief administrator of the judiciary. Its administration is aided by the Judiciary Commission of Louisiana, the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Louisiana_Attorney_Disciplinary_Board&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Louisiana Attorney Disciplinary Board (page does not exist)">Louisiana Attorney Disciplinary Board</a>, and the Judicial Council of the Supreme Court of Louisiana.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="National_Guard">National Guard</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Louisiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: National Guard">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Louisiana has more than 9,000 soldiers in the <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Army_National_Guard" title="Louisiana Army National Guard">Louisiana Army National Guard</a>, including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/225th_Engineer_Brigade" title="225th Engineer Brigade">225th Engineer Brigade</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/256th_Infantry_Brigade" title="256th Infantry Brigade">256th Infantry Brigade</a>. Both these units have served overseas during the <a href="/wiki/War_on_Terror" title="War on Terror">War on Terror</a> in either <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>, <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>, or both. The <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Air_National_Guard" title="Louisiana Air National Guard">Louisiana Air National Guard</a> has over 2,000 airmen and its 159th Fighter Squadron has likewise seen overseas service in combat theaters.</p>
<p>Training sites in the state include <a href="/wiki/Camp_Beauregard" title="Camp Beauregard">Camp Beauregard</a> near <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pineville,_LA" title="Pineville, LA">Pineville</a>, Camp Villere near <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slidell,_LA" title="Slidell, LA">Slidell</a>, Camp Minden near <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Minden,_LA" title="Minden, LA">Minden</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/England_Air_Park" title="England Air Park">England Air Park</a> (formerly <a href="/wiki/England_Air_Force_Base" title="England Air Force Base">England Air Force Base</a>) near <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alexandria,_LA" title="Alexandria, LA">Alexandria</a>, Gillis Long Center near <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carville,_LA" title="Carville, LA">Carville</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jackson_Barracks" title="Jackson Barracks">Jackson Barracks</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans" title="New Orleans">New Orleans</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Louisiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
